<p><b>Shanghai Pudong International Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA</a>: <b>PVG</b>, <a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>ZSPD</b>) is one of two <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airports</a> of <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> and a major aviation hub of China. Pudong Airport mainly serves international flights, while the city's other major airport <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Hongqiao_International_Airport" title="Shanghai Hongqiao International Airport">Shanghai Hongqiao International Airport</a> mainly serves domestic and regional flights. Located about 30 kilometres (19 mi) east of the city center, Pudong Airport occupies a 40-square-kilometre (10,000-acre) site adjacent to the coastline in eastern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pudong_New_Area" title="Pudong New Area">Pudong</a>. The airport is operated by Shanghai Airport Authority (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh">上海机场集团有限公司</span>, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Stock_Exchange" title="Shanghai Stock Exchange">SSE</a>: <a class="external text" href="http://www.sse.com.cn/assortment/stock/list/info/company/index.shtml?COMPANY_CODE=600009" rel="nofollow">600009</a>).</p>
<p>The airport is the main <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a> for <a href="/wiki/China_Eastern_Airlines" title="China Eastern Airlines">China Eastern Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Airlines" title="Shanghai Airlines">Shanghai Airlines</a>, and a major international hub for <a href="/wiki/Air_China" title="Air China">Air China</a>, as well as secondary hub of <a href="/wiki/China_Southern_Airlines" title="China Southern Airlines">China Southern Airlines</a>. It is also the hub for privately owned <a href="/wiki/Juneyao_Airlines" title="Juneyao Airlines">Juneyao Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spring_Airlines" title="Spring Airlines">Spring Airlines</a>, and an Asia-Pacific cargo hub for <a href="/wiki/UPS_Airlines" title="UPS Airlines">UPS</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/DHL_Aviation" title="DHL Aviation">DHL</a>. The DHL hub, opened in July 2012, is said to be the biggest express hub in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pudong Airport has two main passenger terminals, flanked on both sides by four parallel runways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> A third passenger terminal is planned for 2015, in addition to a satellite terminal and two additional runways, raising its annual capacity from 60 million passengers to 80 million, along with the ability to handle six million tonnes of freight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pudong Airport is a fast-growing hub for both passenger and cargo traffic. With 3,275,231 metric tonnes handled in 2015, the airport is the world's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_cargo_traffic" title="World's busiest airports by cargo traffic">third busiest airport</a> by cargo traffic. Pudong Airport also served a total of 60,098,073 passengers in 2015, making it the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/China%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="China's busiest airports by passenger traffic">second busiest airport</a> in mainland China and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">13th busiest</a> in the world. By the end of 2015, Pudong Airport hosted 100 airlines serving 210 destinations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shanghai Pudong is the busiest international hub of <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a>, ranking 22nd globally in terms of international traffic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> although it only provides passenger transfer facilities for a few airlines. About half of its total passenger traffic is international.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pudong Airport is connected to <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Metro" title="Shanghai Metro">Shanghai Metro</a> <a href="/wiki/Line_2,_Shanghai_Metro" title="Line 2, Shanghai Metro">Line 2</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Maglev_Train" title="Shanghai Maglev Train">Shanghai Maglev Train</a> via <a href="/wiki/Pudong_International_Airport_Station" title="Pudong International Airport Station">Pudong International Airport Station</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_development">Early development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Prior to the establishment of Pudong International Airport, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Hongqiao_International_Airport" title="Shanghai Hongqiao International Airport">Shanghai Hongqiao International Airport</a> was the primary airport of Shanghai. During the 1990s, the expansion of Hongqiao Airport to meet growing demand became impossible as the surrounding urban area was developing significantly, and an alternative to assume all international flights had to be sought.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>After deliberation, the municipal government decided to adopt the suggestion from Professor Chen Jiyu of <a href="/wiki/East_China_Normal_University" title="East China Normal University">East China Normal University</a>, who wrote a letter to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Shanghai" title="Mayor of Shanghai">Mayor of Shanghai</a> <a href="/wiki/Xu_Kuangdi" title="Xu Kuangdi">Xu Kuangdi</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> suggesting that the new airport should be constructed on the tidal flats of the south bank of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yangtze_River" title="Yangtze River">Yangtze River</a> estuary, on the coast of the <a href="/wiki/Pudong" title="Pudong">Pudong</a> development zone to the east of Shanghai.</p>
<p>Construction of the first phase of the new Shanghai Pudong International Airport began in October 1997, took two years to build at a cost of RMB 12 billion (1.67 billion USD), and was opened on October 1, 1999.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It covers an area of 40 square kilometres (15 sq mi) and is 30 kilometres (19 mi) from downtown Shanghai. The first phase of the airport has one 4E category runway (4000 m x 60 m) along with two parallel taxiways, an 800,000-square-metre (8,600,000 sq ft) apron, seventy-six aircraft positions and a 50,000 m<sup>2</sup> (540,000 sq ft) cargo warehouse.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>A second runway was opened on March 17, 2005<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, and construction of phase two (including a second terminal, a third runway and a cargo terminal) began in December 2005 and started operation on March 26, 2008, in time for the Beijing <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ongoing_expansion">Ongoing expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ongoing expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In November 2011, Pudong Airport received approval from the national government for a new round of expansion which includes two runways. The 3,800-meter fourth runway, along with an auxiliary taxiway and traffic control facilities, is projected to cost 2.58 billion yuan (USD 403 million). The 3,400-meter fifth runway, along with a new traffic tower, will cost 4.65 billion yuan (USD 726.6 million). Construction was completed in 2015 and has doubled the capacity of the airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The airport has 70 boarding bridges along with 218 parking positions. Four runways are in operation: one 4,000-metre (13,000 ft) runway with 4E rating (capable of accommodating aircraft up to <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a>) and six taxiways, two 3,800-metre (12,500 ft) runways with 4F rating (capable of accommodating aircraft up to <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-8" title="Boeing 747-8">Boeing 747-8</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antonov_An-225" title="Antonov An-225">Antonov An-225</a>) and four taxiways each, and one 3,400-metre (11,200 ft) runway with 4F rating and six taxiways.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_1">Terminal 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Terminal 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Terminal 1 was opened on October 1, 1999 along with a 4000m runway and including a cargo hub.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It was built to handle the demand for traffic and to relieve <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Hongqiao_International_Airport" title="Shanghai Hongqiao International Airport">Shanghai Hongqiao International Airport</a>'s traffic. Terminal 1 is shaped like <a href="/wiki/Kansai_International_Airport" title="Kansai International Airport">Osaka Kansai International Airport</a>'s terminal, but it is shorter and with 28 gates, 13 of which are double decker gates. The exterior of the terminal is shaped like waves. The capacity of Terminal 1 is 20 million passengers. It currently has 204 check-in counters, thirteen luggage conveying belts and covering an area of 280,000 square meters.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2">Terminal 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Terminal 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Terminal 2, opened on March 26, 2008, along with the third runway, gives a capacity of 60 million passengers and 4.2 million tonnes of cargo annually. Terminal 2 is shaped like the 1st terminal but it has more of a wave shaping, rather than a seagull shape and is slightly larger than Terminal 1 and the Terminal 2 have more levels than Terminal 1. Terminal 2 is primarily used by Air China and other <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> members but may be used by <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> airlines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-a1_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-a1-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellite_Concourses">Satellite Concourses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Satellite Concourses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An additional satellite concourse facility to provide further gates and terminal space started construction on December 29, 2015 and is expected to be completed in 2019. This project will support 38 million passengers annually through 83 departure gates across two S1 and S2 concourses. These will be connected by an underground automated <a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">people mover</a> to the current T1 and T2 terminals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transportation">Ground transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ground transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_maglev_train_coming_out,_Pudong_International_Airport,_Shanghai.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1259" data-file-width="2338" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/A_maglev_train_coming_out%2C_Pudong_International_Airport%2C_Shanghai.jpg/220px-A_maglev_train_coming_out%2C_Pudong_International_Airport%2C_Shanghai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/A_maglev_train_coming_out%2C_Pudong_International_Airport%2C_Shanghai.jpg/330px-A_maglev_train_coming_out%2C_Pudong_International_Airport%2C_Shanghai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/A_maglev_train_coming_out%2C_Pudong_International_Airport%2C_Shanghai.jpg/440px-A_maglev_train_coming_out%2C_Pudong_International_Airport%2C_Shanghai.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Highway">Highway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Highway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>North: <a href="/wiki/S1_Yingbin_Expressway" title="S1 Yingbin Expressway">S1 Yingbin Expressway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huaxia_Elevated_Road" title="Huaxia Elevated Road">Huaxia Elevated Road</a></li>
<li>South: <a href="/wiki/Shanghai%E2%80%93Jiaxing%E2%80%93Huzhou_Expressway" title="Shanghai–Jiaxing–Huzhou Expressway">Shanghai–Jiaxing–Huzhou Expressway</a> and <a href="/wiki/G1501_Shanghai_Ring_Expressway" title="G1501 Shanghai Ring Expressway">G1501 Shanghai Ring Expressway</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maglev_train">Maglev train</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Maglev train">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Starting service on January 29, 2004 as the first commercial high-speed maglev railway in the world, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Maglev_Train" title="Shanghai Maglev Train">Shanghai Maglev Train</a> links Pudong International Airport with <a href="/wiki/Longyang_Road_Station" title="Longyang Road Station">Longyang Road Metro Station</a>, where transfer to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_Metro_Line_2" title="Shanghai Metro Line 2">Line 2</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_Metro_Line_7" title="Shanghai Metro Line 7">Line 7</a>, and Line 16 is possible. The 30-km ride from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Longyang_Road_(Shanghai_Metro)" title="Longyang Road (Shanghai Metro)">Longyang Road Metro station</a> to Pudong International Airport typically takes less than eight minutes, with the maximum speed reaching 431 km/h. Trains operate every 15 minutes; therefore passengers can expect to arrive in less than 25 minutes, waiting time included.</p>
<p>All cars are equipped with racks and space designated for luggage.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shanghai_Metro_Line_2">Shanghai Metro Line 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Shanghai Metro Line 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_Metro_Line_2" title="Shanghai Metro Line 2">Shanghai Metro Line 2</a> also provides service between Pudong International Airport and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Longyang_Road_(Shanghai_Metro)" title="Longyang Road (Shanghai Metro)">Longyang Road</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lujiazui_(Shanghai_Metro)" title="Lujiazui (Shanghai Metro)">Lujiazui</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Square_(Shanghai_Metro)" title="People's Square (Shanghai Metro)">People's Square</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Hongqiao_International_Airport" title="Shanghai Hongqiao International Airport">Hongqiao International Airport</a>, Shanghai's primary domestic airport as well as <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Hongqiao_Railway_Station" title="Shanghai Hongqiao Railway Station">Shanghai Hongqiao Railway Station</a>. Line 2 is part of the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Metro" title="Shanghai Metro">Shanghai Metro</a> system; therefore unlike the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Maglev_Train" title="Shanghai Maglev Train">Maglev</a>, free in-system transfer to other lines are possible.</p>
<p>Prices are substantially lower than the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Maglev_Train" title="Shanghai Maglev Train">Maglev</a>. A casual ride to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Square_(Shanghai_Metro)" title="People's Square (Shanghai Metro)">People's Square</a>, the city center, typically takes just over one hour. It is wise to allow more than five hours for a safe flight transfer at <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Hongqiao_International_Airport" title="Shanghai Hongqiao International Airport">Hongqiao International Airport</a> using public transportation.</p>
<p>It should further be noted that Line 2 operates in two sections: trains from Pudong International Airport terminate at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guanglan_Road_(Shanghai_Metro)" title="Guanglan Road (Shanghai Metro)">Guanglan Road</a>, where passengers wishing to travel on change trains across the platform. In addition, not all trains go to <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Hongqiao_International_Airport" title="Shanghai Hongqiao International Airport">Hongqiao International Airport</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport_buses">Airport buses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Airport buses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shanghai_Pudong_Airport_T1-T2bus.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Shanghai_Pudong_Airport_T1-T2bus.JPG/220px-Shanghai_Pudong_Airport_T1-T2bus.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Shanghai_Pudong_Airport_T1-T2bus.JPG/330px-Shanghai_Pudong_Airport_T1-T2bus.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Shanghai_Pudong_Airport_T1-T2bus.JPG/440px-Shanghai_Pudong_Airport_T1-T2bus.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shanghai_Pudong_Airport_T1-T2bus.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Shanghai Pudong Airport Bus Expressway</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Eight airport bus lines serve Pudong International Airport, providing rapid links to various destinations.</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Airport Bus Route 1:</b> To <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Hongqiao_Railway_Station" title="Shanghai Hongqiao Railway Station">Shanghai Hongqiao Railway Station</a> via <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Hongqiao_International_Airport" title="Shanghai Hongqiao International Airport">Shanghai Hongqiao International Airport</a></li>
<li><b>Airport Bus Route 2:</b> To <a href="/wiki/Jing%27an_Temple" title="Jing'an Temple">Jing'an Temple</a> (City Terminal Hub)</li>
<li><b>Airport Bus Route 4:</b> To <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hongkou_Stadium" title="Hongkou Stadium">Hongkou Stadium</a> Hub (Huayuan Road), via Deping Road at Pudong Avenue, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wujiaochang" title="Wujiaochang">Wujiaochang</a> and Dabaishu.</li>
<li><b>Airport Bus Route 5:</b> To <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Railway_Station" title="Shanghai Railway Station">Shanghai Railway Station</a>, via <a href="/wiki/Longyang_Road_Station" title="Longyang Road Station">Longyang Road Metro Station</a>, Century Avenue at South Pudong Road (<a href="/wiki/Lujiazui" title="Lujiazui">Lujiazui</a>) and East Yan'an Road at Middle Zhejiang Road (<a href="/wiki/People%27s_Square" title="People's Square">People's Square</a>)</li>
<li><b>Airport Bus Route 7:</b> To <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_South_Railway_Station" title="Shanghai South Railway Station">Shanghai South Railway Station</a>, via West Huaxia Road at Shangnan Road and East Huaxia Road at Chuansha Road (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chuansha" title="Chuansha">Chuansha</a>).</li>
<li><b>Airport Bus Route 8:</b> To <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanhui" title="Nanhui">Nanhui</a> Coach &amp; Bus Station</li>
<li><b>Airport Bus Route 9:</b> To <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xinzhuang_Metro_Station" title="Xinzhuang Metro Station">Xinzhuang Metro Station</a></li>
<li><b>Airport Bus Ring Route 1:</b> To Hangchengyuan (Shiwan), via stops in Airport Workplace.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shanghai_Pudong_International_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>On November 28, 2009, <a href="/wiki/Avient_Aviation_Flight_324" title="Avient Aviation Flight 324">Avient Aviation Flight 324</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Avient_Aviation" title="Avient Aviation">Avient Aviation</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-11F" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-11F">McDonnell Douglas MD-11F</a> cargo plane registered to <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> (registration: Z-BAV) departing for <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/28_November_2009_Avient_crash" title="28 November 2009 Avient crash">crashed into a warehouse near the runway of the airport</a> due to a <a href="/wiki/Tailstrike" title="Tailstrike">tailstrike</a> that caught fire during takeoff and broke into several pieces with seven people on board. Three people died and four were injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></li>
<li>In the afternoon of June 12, 2016, at the C check-in area of Terminal 2 of the airport, a man used a homemade firecracker to create an explosion. Four people were injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The police identified the suspect is a 29-year-old man from <a href="/wiki/Guizhou" title="Guizhou">Guizhou</a> Province, named Zhou Xingbai (周兴柏).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
